<p>The <b>Democratic Party</b> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Partito Democratico</i></span>, <b>PD</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CollinMartin2012_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-CollinMartin2012-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paquino2013_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paquino2013-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Italy" title="List of political parties in Italy">political party in Italy</a>.</p>
<p>The party's leader is <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, who was elected as national secretary in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2013" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2013">2013 leadership election</a> (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Secretaries_of_the_Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="List of Secretaries of the Democratic Party (Italy)">leaders' list</a>).</p>
<p>The PD was founded on 14 October 2007 as a merger of various <a href="/wiki/Centre-left_politics" title="Centre-left politics">centre-left</a> parties which had been part of <a href="/wiki/The_Union_(Italy)" title="The Union (Italy)">The Union</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2006" title="Italian general election, 2006">2006 general election</a>. At foundation the majority of the PD was formed by the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> (heirs of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Italian Communist Party</a>) and the largely <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>-inspired <a href="/wiki/Democracy_is_Freedom_%E2%80%93_The_Daisy" title="Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy">Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slomp2011_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slomp2011-12">[12]</a></sup> Within the party, an important role is thus played by <a href="/wiki/Christian_left" title="Christian left">Christian leftists</a>, who are direct heirs of the former <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a>'s left-wing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2013" title="Italian general election, 2013">2013 general election</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (Italy)">2014 European Parliament election</a>, the PD was the largest party in the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Italy)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Italy)">Chamber of Deputies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Republic_(Italy)" title="Senate of the Republic (Italy)">Senate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, respectively. As of 2015, other than the national government, Democrats head fifteen <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Italy" title="Regions of Italy">regional</a> governments out of twenty and function as coalition partner in <a href="/wiki/Trentino-Alto_Adige/S%C3%BCdtirol" title="Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol">Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol</a>.</p>
<p>From 2013 the Italian <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Italy)" title="Council of Ministers (Italy)">government</a> has been consequently led by three successive Democratic <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Prime Ministers</a>: <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a> (<a href="/wiki/Letta_Cabinet" title="Letta Cabinet">Letta Cabinet</a>, 2013–2014), Matteo Renzi (<a href="/wiki/Renzi_Cabinet" title="Renzi Cabinet">Renzi Cabinet</a>, 2014–2016), and <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gentiloni_Cabinet" title="Gentiloni Cabinet">Gentiloni Cabinet</a>, 2016–present).</p>
<p>Other prominent Democrats include <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massimo_D%27Alema" title="Massimo D'Alema">Massimo D'Alema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piero_Fassino" title="Piero Fassino">Piero Fassino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graziano_Delrio" title="Graziano Delrio">Graziano Delrio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Elena_Boschi" title="Maria Elena Boschi">Maria Elena Boschi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debora_Serracchiani" title="Debora Serracchiani">Debora Serracchiani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Guerini" title="Lorenzo Guerini">Lorenzo Guerini</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ettore_Rosato&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ettore Rosato (page does not exist)">Ettore Rosato</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luigi_Zanda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luigi Zanda (page does not exist)">Luigi Zanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Chiamparino" title="Sergio Chiamparino">Sergio Chiamparino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Bonaccini" title="Stefano Bonaccini">Stefano Bonaccini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Rossi_(politician)" title="Enrico Rossi (politician)">Enrico Rossi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Zingaretti" title="Nicola Zingaretti">Nicola Zingaretti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_De_Luca" title="Vincenzo De Luca">Vincenzo De Luca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michele_Emiliano" title="Michele Emiliano">Michele Emiliano</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Epifani" title="Guglielmo Epifani">Guglielmo Epifani</a>. Former bigwigs include <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Napolitano" title="Giorgio Napolitano">Giorgio Napolitano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Mattarella" title="Sergio Mattarella">Sergio Mattarella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giuliano_Amato" title="Giuliano Amato">Giuliano Amato</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Rutelli" title="Francesco Rutelli">Francesco Rutelli</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2>Contents</h2>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background:_The_Olive_Tree">Background: The Olive Tree</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background: The Olive Tree">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Olive_Tree_(Italy)" title="The Olive Tree (Italy)">The Olive Tree (Italy)</a></div>
<p>In the early 1990s, following <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangentopoli" title="Tangentopoli">Tangentopoli</a></i>, the end of the so-called <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Italian_Republic" title="History of the Italian Republic">First Republic</a> and the transformation of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Italian Communist Party</a> (PCI) into the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_the_Left" title="Democratic Party of the Left">Democratic Party of the Left</a> (PDS), a process aimed at uniting left-wing and centre-left forces into a single political entity was started.</p>
<p>In 1995 <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Italian_Minister_of_Economic_Development" title="Italian Minister of Economic Development">minister of Industry</a> on behalf of the left-wing faction of <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a> (DC), entered politics and founded <a href="/wiki/The_Olive_Tree_(Italy)" title="The Olive Tree (Italy)">The Olive Tree</a> (<i>L'Ulivo</i>), a centre-left coalition including the PDS, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_People%27s_Party_(1994)" title="Italian People's Party (1994)">Italian People's Party</a> (PPI), the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_Greens" title="Federation of the Greens">Federation of the Greens</a> (FdV), <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renewal" title="Italian Renewal">Italian Renewal</a> (RI), the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialists" title="Italian Socialists">Italian Socialists</a> (SI) and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Union_(Italy)" title="Democratic Union (Italy)">Democratic Union</a> (UD). The coalition, in alliance with the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Refoundation_Party" title="Communist Refoundation Party">Communist Refoundation Party</a> (PRC), won the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_1996" title="Italian general election, 1996">1996 general election</a> and Prodi became Prime Minister.</p>
<p>In February 1998 the PDS merged with minor centre-left parties to become the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> (DS), while in March 2002 the PPI, RI and <a href="/wiki/The_Democrats_(Italy)" title="The Democrats (Italy)">The Democrats</a> (Prodi's own party, launched in 1999) became <a href="/wiki/Democracy_is_Freedom_%E2%80%93_The_Daisy" title="Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy">Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy</a> (DL). In the summer of 2003, Romano Prodi suggested that the centre-left forces would participate in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2004_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2004 (Italy)">2004 European Parliament election</a> with a common list. Whereas the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Democrats_for_Europe" title="Union of Democrats for Europe">Union of Democrats for Europe</a> (UDEUR) and the far-left parties refused the offer, four parties accepted it: the DS, DL, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Democratic_Socialists" title="Italian Democratic Socialists">Italian Democratic Socialists</a> (SDI) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Republicans_Movement" title="European Republicans Movement">European Republicans Movement</a> (MRE). They launched a joint list named "United in the Olive Tree" (<i>Uniti nell'Ulivo</i>) which ran in the election and garnered 31.1% of the vote. The project was later abandoned in 2005 by the SDI.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2006" title="Italian general election, 2006">2006 general election</a> the list obtained 31.3% of the vote for the Chamber of Deputies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_to_the_Democratic_Party">Road to the Democratic Party</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Road to the Democratic Party">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_(2c).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1933" data-file-width="1517" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_%282c%29.jpg/150px-Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_%282c%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_%282c%29.jpg/225px-Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_%282c%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_%282c%29.jpg/300px-Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_%282c%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romano_Prodi_in_Nova_Gorica_(2c).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The project of a "Democratic Party" was often mentioned by Prodi as the natural evolution of The Olive Tree and was envisioned in a 2003 appeal in <i><a href="/wiki/Il_Foglio" title="Il Foglio">Il Foglio</a></i> by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Michele_Salvati&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Michele Salvati (page does not exist)">Michele Salvati</a>, a former centrist deputy of the DS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The term <i>Partito Democratico</i> was used for the first time in a formal context by the DL and DS members of the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Council_of_Veneto" title="Regional Council of Veneto">Regional Council</a> of <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a>, who chose to form a joint group named The Olive Tree – Venetian Democratic Party (<i>L'Ulivo – Partito Democratico Veneto</i>) in March 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2006 election result, anticipated by the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Primary_elections_in_Italy" title="Primary elections in Italy">primary election</a> in which over four million voters endorsed Prodi as candidate for Prime Minister, gave a push to the project of a unified centre-left party. <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Rutelli" title="Francesco Rutelli">Francesco Rutelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piero_Fassino" title="Piero Fassino">Piero Fassino</a>, party leaders of DL and the DS respectively, scheduled their parties' congresses for April 2007 in order to formally approve the merger.</p>
<p>On 19 April 2007 the DS held their final party congress, during which approximately 75% of party members voted in support of the merger into the PD. The left-wing opposition, led by <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Mussi" title="Fabio Mussi">Fabio Mussi</a>, obtained just 15% of the support within the party. A third motion, presented by <a href="/wiki/Gavino_Angius" title="Gavino Angius">Gavino Angius</a> and supportive of the PD only within the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a> (PES), obtained 10% of the vote. During and following the congress, both Mussi and Angius announced their intention not to join the PD and founded a new party called <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Italy)" title="Democratic Left (Italy)">Democratic Left</a> (SD).</p>
<p>On 22 May 2007 the composition of the organising committee of the nascent party was announced. It featured 45 members, mainly politicians from the two major parties involved in the process, but included also external figures such as <a href="/wiki/Marco_Follini" title="Marco Follini">Marco Follini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottaviano_Del_Turco" title="Ottaviano Del Turco">Ottaviano Del Turco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luciana_Sbarbati" title="Luciana Sbarbati">Luciana Sbarbati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renato_Soru" title="Renato Soru">Renato Soru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giuliano_Amato" title="Giuliano Amato">Giuliano Amato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gad_Lerner" title="Gad Lerner">Gad Lerner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tullia_Zevi" title="Tullia Zevi">Tullia Zevi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> On 18 June the committee met to decide the rules for the open election of the 2,400 members of the party's constituent assembly. Prodi announced each voter would choose between a number of lists, each of them associated with a candidate for secretary.</p>
<p>Eight parties agreed to merge into the PD:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> (<a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Democracy_is_Freedom_%E2%80%93_The_Daisy" title="Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy">Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Democratic_Party" title="Southern Democratic Party">Southern Democratic Party</a> (centrist);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sardinia_Project" title="Sardinia Project">Sardinia Project</a> (social-democratic);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Republicans_Movement" title="European Republicans Movement">European Republicans Movement</a> (<a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">social-liberal</a>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republicans_(Italy)" title="Democratic Republicans (Italy)">Democratic Republicans</a> (social-liberal);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middle_Italy_(political_party)" title="Middle Italy (political party)">Middle Italy</a> (centrist);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reformist_Alliance" title="Reformist Alliance">Reformist Alliance</a> (social-democratic).</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_leadership_election">Foundation and leadership election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foundation and leadership election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2007" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2007">Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2007</a></div>
<p>All candidates interested in running for the PD leadership had to be associated with one of the founding parties and present at least 2,000 valid signatures by 30 July 2007. A total of ten candidates officially registered their candidacy: <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Furio_Colombo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Furio Colombo (page does not exist)">Furio Colombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marco_Pannella" title="Marco Pannella">Marco Pannella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Di_Pietro" title="Antonio Di Pietro">Antonio Di Pietro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Adinolfi" title="Mario Adinolfi">Mario Adinolfi</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pier_Giorgio_Gawronski&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pier Giorgio Gawronski (page does not exist)">Pier Giorgio Gawronski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacopo_Schettini_Gherardini" title="Jacopo Schettini Gherardini">Jacopo Schettini</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lucio_Cangini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lucio Cangini (page does not exist)">Lucio Cangini</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amerigo_Rutigliano&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amerigo Rutigliano (page does not exist)">Amerigo Rutigliano</a>. Of these, Pannella and Di Pietro were rejected because of their involvement in external parties (the Radicals and <a href="/wiki/Italy_of_Values" title="Italy of Values">Italy of Values</a> respectively), whereas Cangini and Rutigliano did not manage to present the necessary 2,000 valid signatures for the 9pm deadline, and Colombo's candidacy was instead made into hiatus in order to give him 48 additional hours to integrate the required documentation; Colombo later decided to retire his candidacy citing his impossibility to fit with all the requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colombo_retired_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-colombo_retired-19">[19]</a></sup> All rejected candidates had the chance against the decision in 48 hours' time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> with Pannella and Rutigliano being the only two candidates to appeal against it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Both were rejected on 3 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 October 2007 Veltroni was elected leader with about 75% of the national votes in an <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">open primary</a> attended by over three million voters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Veltroni was proclaimed secretary during a party's constituent assembly held in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> on 28 October 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 November, the new logo was unveiled; it depicts the party acronym PD with colours reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Italy" title="Flag of Italy">Italian tricolour flag</a> (green, white and red) and features an <a href="/wiki/Olive_branch" title="Olive branch">olive branch</a>, the historical symbol of The Olive Tree. In the words of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ermete_Realacci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ermete Realacci (page does not exist)">Ermete Realacci</a>, green represents the ecologist and social-liberal cultures, white is for the Catholic solidarity and red for the socialist and social-democratic traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The "green-white-red" idea was coined by Schettini during his campaign.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_of_Walter_Veltroni">Leadership of Walter Veltroni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Leadership of Walter Veltroni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="356" data-file-width="283" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg/150px-Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg/225px-Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Walter_Veltroni_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the premature fall of the <a href="/wiki/Prodi_II_Cabinet" title="Prodi II Cabinet">Prodi II Cabinet</a> in January 2008, the PD decided to form a less diverse coalition. The party proposed to the Radicals and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party_(2007)" title="Italian Socialist Party (2007)">Socialist Party</a> (PS) to join its lists, but only the Radicals accepted, and formed an alliance with Italy of Values (IdV), which was set to join the PD after the election. The PD included many notable candidates and new faces in its lists and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a>, who tried to present the PD as the party of the renewal in contrast both with <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a> and the previous centre-left government, ran an intense and modern campaign, which led him to visit all <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Italy" title="Provinces of Italy">provinces of Italy</a>, but that was not enough.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2008" title="Italian general election, 2008">2008 general election</a> on 13–14 April 2008 the PD–IdV coalition won 37.5% of the vote and was defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Centre-right_coalition" title="Centre-right coalition">centre-right coalition</a>, composed of <a href="/wiki/The_People_of_Freedom" title="The People of Freedom">The People of Freedom</a> (PdL), <a href="/wiki/Lega_Nord" title="Lega Nord">Lega Nord</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Autonomy" title="Movement for the Autonomy">Movement for the Autonomy</a> (46.8%). The PD was able to absorb some votes from the parties of the far left (as also IdV did), but lost voters to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Centre_(2008)" title="Union of the Centre (2008)">Union of the Centre</a> (UdC), ending up with 33.2% of the vote, 217 deputies and 119 senators. After the election Veltroni, who was gratified by the result, formed a <a href="/wiki/Shadow_Cabinet_of_Italy_(2008)" title="Shadow Cabinet of Italy (2008)">shadow cabinet</a>. IdV, excited by its 4.4% which made it the fourth largest party in Parliament, refused to join both the Democratic groups and the shadow cabinet.</p>
<p>The early months after the election were a difficult time for the PD and Veltroni, whose leadership was weakened by the growing influence of internal factions, because of the popularity of Berlusconi and the dramatic rise of IdV in opinion polls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> IdV became a strong competitor of the PD and the relations between the two parties became tense. In the <a href="/wiki/Abruzzo_regional_election,_2008" title="Abruzzo regional election, 2008">2008 Abruzzo regional election</a> the PD was forced to support IdV candidate <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carlo_Costantini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carlo Costantini (page does not exist)">Carlo Costantini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In October Veltroni, who distanced from Di Pietro many times, declared that "on some issues he [Di Pietro] is distant from the democratic language of the centre-left".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_of_Dario_Franceschini">Leadership of Dario Franceschini</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Leadership of Dario Franceschini">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dario_Franceschini_daticamera.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="228" data-file-width="165" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dario_Franceschini_daticamera.jpg/150px-Dario_Franceschini_daticamera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Dario_Franceschini_daticamera.jpg 1.5x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dario_Franceschini_daticamera.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2009, after a crushing defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_regional_election,_2009" title="Sardinian regional election, 2009">Sardinian regional election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a> resigned as party secretary and was replaced by his deputy <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a> on an interim basis to guide the party toward the selection of a new stable leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-sec-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opposition_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-opposition-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opposition_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-opposition-30">[30]</a></sup> Franceschini was elected by the party's national assembly with 1,047 votes out of 1,258. His only opponent <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Parisi" title="Arturo Parisi">Arturo Parisi</a> won a mere 92 votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-sec-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opposition_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-opposition-30">[30]</a></sup> Franceschini was the first former <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democrat</a> to lead the party.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (Italy)">2009 European Parliament election</a> was an important test for the PD. Prior to the election, the PD considered offering hospitality to the Socialist Party (PS) and the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_Greens" title="Federation of the Greens">Greens</a> in its lists, and proposed a similar pact to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Italy)" title="Democratic Left (Italy)">Democratic Left</a> (SD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> However, the Socialists, the Greens and Democratic Left decided instead to contest the election together as a new alliance called <a href="/wiki/Left_Ecology_Freedom" title="Left Ecology Freedom">Left and Freedom</a>, which failed to achieve the 4% threshold required to return any MEPs, but damaged the PD, which gained 26.1% of the vote, returning 21 MEPs.</p>
<p>The national congress and the subsequent leadership primary were announced for October. By July three candidates announced their bid: <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ignazio_Marino" title="Ignazio Marino">Ignazio Marino</a> and the outgoing secretary Dario Franceschini.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_of_Pier_Luigi_Bersani">Leadership of Pier Luigi Bersani</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Leadership of Pier Luigi Bersani">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2009" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2009">Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2009</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="288" data-file-width="232" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png/150px-Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png/225px-Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9f/Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pier_Luigi_Bersani_cropped.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the local congresses a 56.4% of party members voted and Bersani was by far the most voted candidate with 55.1% of the vote, largely ahead of Franceschini (37.0%) and Marino (7.9%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On 25 October 2009, Bersani was elected new secretary of the party with about 53% of the vote in an open primary in which three million people participated. Franceschini got 34% and Marino 13%. On 7 November, during the first meeting of the new national assembly, Bersani was declared secretary, <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a> was elected party president (with <a href="/wiki/Marina_Sereni" title="Marina Sereni">Marina Sereni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Scalfarotto" title="Ivan Scalfarotto">Ivan Scalfarotto</a> vice-presidents), <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a> deputy secretary and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Antonio_Misiani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Antonio Misiani (page does not exist)">Antonio Misiani</a> treasurer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In reaction to the election of Bersani, perceived by some moderates as an old-style social democrat, <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Rutelli" title="Francesco Rutelli">Francesco Rutelli</a>, a long-time critic of the party's course, and other centrists and liberals within the PD left in order to form a new centrist party, named <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Italy" title="Alliance for Italy">Alliance for Italy</a> (ApI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Following March 2009, and especially after Bersani's victory, many deputies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> senators,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> one MEP and several regional/local councillors<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> left the party to join the UdC, ApI and other minor parties: they included many <i><a href="/wiki/Rutelliani" title="Rutelliani">Rutelliani</a></i> and most <a href="/wiki/Theo-Dems" title="Theo-Dems">Theo-Dems</a>.</p>
<p>In March 2010 a <a href="/wiki/Italian_regional_elections,_2010" title="Italian regional elections, 2010">big round of regional elections</a>, involving eleven regions, took place. The PD lost four regions to the centre-right (<a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_regional_election,_2010" title="Piedmontese regional election, 2010">Piedmont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lazio_regional_election,_2010" title="Lazio regional election, 2010">Lazio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campania_regional_election,_2010" title="Campania regional election, 2010">Campania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calabrian_regional_election,_2010" title="Calabrian regional election, 2010">Calabria</a>), and maintained its hold on six (<a href="/wiki/Ligurian_regional_election,_2010" title="Ligurian regional election, 2010">Liguria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emilia-Romagna_regional_election,_2010" title="Emilia-Romagna regional election, 2010">Emilia-Romagna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_regional_election,_2010" title="Tuscan regional election, 2010">Tuscany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marche_regional_election,_2010" title="Marche regional election, 2010">Marche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umbrian_regional_election,_2010" title="Umbrian regional election, 2010">Umbria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basilicata_regional_election,_2010" title="Basilicata regional election, 2010">Basilicata</a>), plus <a href="/wiki/Apulian_regional_election,_2010" title="Apulian regional election, 2010">Apulia</a>, a traditionally conservative region where, due to divisions within the centre-right, <a href="/wiki/Nichi_Vendola" title="Nichi Vendola">Nichi Vendola</a> of SEL was re-elected with the PD's support.</p>
<p>In September 2011 Bersani was invited by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Di_Pietro" title="Antonio Di Pietro">Antonio Di Pietro</a>'s IdV to take part to its annual late summer convention in <a href="/wiki/Vasto" title="Vasto">Vasto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abruzzo" title="Abruzzo">Abruzzo</a>. Bersani, who had been accused by Di Pietro of avoiding him in order to court the centre-right UdC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> proposed the formation of a "New Olive Tree" coalition comprising the PD, IdV and SEL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The three party leaders agreed in what was soon dubbed the "pact of Vasto".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> However, after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resignation_of_Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Resignation of Silvio Berlusconi">resignation of Silvio Berlusconi</a> as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Prime Minister</a> in November 2011, the PD gave external support to <a href="/wiki/Mario_Monti" title="Mario Monti">Mario Monti</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Monti_Cabinet" title="Monti Cabinet">technocratic government</a>, along with the PdL and the UdC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> effectively broking with IdV and SEL.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_to_the_2013_general_election">Road to the 2013 general election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Road to the 2013 general election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Italian_centre-left_primary_election,_2012" title="Italian centre-left primary election, 2012">Italian centre-left primary election, 2012</a></div>
<p>A year after the "pact of Vasto", the relations between the PD and IdV had become tense. IdV and its leader, Antonio Di Pietro, were thus excluded from the coalition talks led by Bersani. To these talks were instead invited SEL, led by <a href="/wiki/Nichi_Vendola" title="Nichi Vendola">Nichi Vendola</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party_(2007)" title="Italian Socialist Party (2007)">Italian Socialist Party</a> (PSI), led by <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Nencini" title="Riccardo Nencini">Riccardo Nencini</a>. The talks resulted, on 13 October 2012, in the "Pact of Democrats and Progressives" (later known as <a href="/wiki/Italy._Common_Good" title="Italy. Common Good">Italy. Common Good</a>) and produced the rules for the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Italian_centre-left_primary_election,_2012" title="Italian centre-left primary election, 2012">centre-left primary election</a>, during which the PD–SEL–PSI joint candidate for Prime Minister in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2013" title="Italian general election, 2013">2013 general election</a> would be selected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the primary the strongest challenge to Bersani was posed by a fellow Democrat, the 37-year-old mayor of <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> moderniser, who had officially launched his leadership bid on 13 September 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archiviostorico.corriere.it_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-archiviostorico.corriere.it-47">[47]</a></sup> Bersani launched his own bid on 14 October in his hometown <a href="/wiki/Bettola" title="Bettola">Bettola</a>, north-western <a href="/wiki/Emilia_(region_of_Italy)" title="Emilia (region of Italy)">Emilia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Other candidates included Nichi Vendola (SEL),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Tabacci" title="Bruno Tabacci">Bruno Tabacci</a> (ApI), and <a href="/wiki/Laura_Puppato" title="Laura Puppato">Laura Puppato</a> (PD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the meantime, in the <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_regional_election,_2012" title="Sicilian regional election, 2012">2012 regional election</a> <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Crocetta" title="Rosario Crocetta">Rosario Crocetta</a>, a Democrat, was elected President with 30.5% of the vote thanks to the support of the UdC, but the coalition failed to secure an outright majority in the Regional Assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> For the first time in 50 years, a man of the left had the chance to govern Sicily.</p>
<p>On 25 November Bersani came ahead in the first round of the primary election with 44.9% of the vote, Renzi came second with 35.5%, followed by Vendola (15.6%), Puppato (2.6%) and Tabacci (1.4%). Bersani did better in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">South</a>, while Renzi prevailed in <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umbria" title="Umbria">Umbria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marche" title="Marche">Marche</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In the subsequent run-off, on 2 December, Bersani trounced Renzi 60.9% to 39.1%, by winning in each and every single region but Tuscany, where Renzi won 54.9% of the vote. The PD secretary did particularly well in <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a> (67.8%), <a href="/wiki/Campania" title="Campania">Campania</a> (69.4%), <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">Apulia</a> (71.4%), <a href="/wiki/Basilicata" title="Basilicata">Basilicata</a> (71.7%), <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabria</a> (74.4%), <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> (66.5%), and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> (73.5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_general_election_and_aftermath">2013 general election and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2013 general election and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2013" title="Italian general election, 2013">Italian general election, 2013</a>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_presidential_election,_2013" title="Italian presidential election, 2013">Italian presidential election, 2013</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Letta_Cabinet" title="Letta Cabinet">Letta Cabinet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="347" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg/150px-Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg/225px-Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg/300px-Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enrico_Letta_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the election the PD and its coalition fared much worse than expected and according to pollsters predictions. The PD won just 25.4% of the vote for the Chamber of Deputies (–8.0% from 2008) and the centre-left coalition narrowly won the majority in the house over the centre-right coalition (29.5% to 29.3%). Even worse, in the Senate the PD and its allies failed to get an outright majority, due to the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Five_Star_Movement" title="Five Star Movement">Five Star Movement</a> (M5S) and the centre-right's victory in key regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campania" title="Campania">Campania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">Apulia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> (the centre-right was awarded of the majority premium in those regions, leaving the centre-left with just a handful of elects there). As a result, Bersani, who refused any agreement with the PdL and was rejected by the M5S, failed to form a government.</p>
<p>On 17 April, after an agreement with the centre-right parties, Bersani put forward <a href="/wiki/Franco_Marini" title="Franco Marini">Franco Marini</a> as his party's <a href="/wiki/Italian_presidential_election,_2013" title="Italian presidential election, 2013">candidate for President</a> to succeed to <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Napolitano" title="Giorgio Napolitano">Giorgio Napolitano</a>. However, Renzi, several Democratic delegates and SEL announced that they would not support Marini.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> On 18 April Marini received just 521 votes in the first ballot, short of the 672 needed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parlamento_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parlamento-58">[58]</a></sup> as more than 200 centre-left delegates rebelled. On 19 April the PD and SEL selected <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a> to be their candidate in the fourth ballot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Despite his candidacy had received unanimous support among the two parties' delegates, Prodi obtained only 395 votes in the fourth ballot<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parlamento_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Parlamento-58">[58]</a></sup> as more than 100 centre-left electors did not vote for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> After the vote, Prodi pulled out of the race and Bersani announced his resignation from party secretary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Also Bindi, the party's president, announced her resignation as she did not want to carry responsibility for the party's bad management during the past weeks. The day after Napolitano accepted to stand again for election and was re-elected President with the support of most parliamentary parties.</p>
<p>On 28 April <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a>, the party's deputy secretary and former <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democrat</a>, was sworn in as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Prime Minister of Italy</a> at the head of a <a href="/wiki/Letta_Cabinet" title="Letta Cabinet">government</a> based around a <a href="/wiki/Grand_coalition" title="Grand coalition">grand coalition</a> including the PdL, <a href="/wiki/Civic_Choice" title="Civic Choice">Civic Choice</a> (SC) and the UdC. Letta was the first Democrat to become Prime Minister.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_of_Guglielmo_Epifani">Leadership of Guglielmo Epifani</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Leadership of Guglielmo Epifani">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guglielmo_Epifani_daticamera.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="228" data-file-width="165" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Guglielmo_Epifani_daticamera.jpg/150px-Guglielmo_Epifani_daticamera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Guglielmo_Epifani_daticamera.jpg 1.5x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guglielmo_Epifani_daticamera.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Epifani" title="Guglielmo Epifani">Guglielmo Epifani</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Bersani's resignation from party secretary on 20 April 2013, the PD remained without a leader for two weeks.</p>
<p>On 11 May 2013 at the national assembly of the party <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Epifani" title="Guglielmo Epifani">Guglielmo Epifani</a> was elected secretary with 85.8% of vote. Epifani, secretary-general of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_General_Confederation_of_Labour" title="Italian General Confederation of Labour">Italian General Confederation of Labour</a> (CGIL), Italy's largest trade union, from 2002 to 2010, was the first former <a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party" title="Italian Socialist Party">Socialist</a> to lead the party. Epifani's mission was to lead the party toward a national congress in October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>A few weeks after Epifani's election as secretary, the PD had a success in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_local_election,_2013" title="Italian local election, 2013">2013 local elections</a>, winning in 69 <i><a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">comuni</a></i> (including <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> and all the other 14 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Italy" title="Provinces of Italy">provincial</a> capitals up for election), while the PdL won 22 and the M5S 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 November Epifani announced that the PD would organise the next congress of the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a> (PES) in Rome in early 2014, sparking protests among some of the party's Christian democrats, who opposed PES membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Epifani was however little more than a secretary <i>pro tempore</i> and, in fact, he frequently repeated that he was not going to run for a full term as secretary in the leadership race that would take place in late 2013, saying that his candidacy would be a betrayal of his mandate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Four individuals filed their bid on 11 October: <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Civati" title="Giuseppe Civati">Pippo Civati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Cuperlo" title="Gianni Cuperlo">Gianni Cuperlo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Pittella" title="Gianni Pittella">Gianni Pittella</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Repubblica-2013-10-11_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Repubblica-2013-10-11-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_of_Matteo_Renzi">Leadership of Matteo Renzi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Leadership of Matteo Renzi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2013" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2013">Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2013</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="431" data-file-width="331" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg/150px-Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg/225px-Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg/300px-Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matteo_Renzi_crop_2015.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As usual, the leadership race started with voting by party members in local conventions (7–17 November). Renzi came first with 45.3%, followed by Cuperlo (39.4%), Civati (9.4%) and Pittella (5.8%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The first three were thus admitted to the open primary.</p>
<p>On 8 December Renzi, who won in all regions but was stronger in the Centre-North, trounced his opponents with 67.6% of the vote. Cuperlo, whose support was higher in the South, came second with 18.2%, while Civati, whose message did well with northern urban and progressive voters, third with 14.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On 15 December Renzi, whose executive included many young people and a majority of women,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> was proclaimed secretary by the party's national assembly, while Cuperlo was elected president, as proposed by Renzi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 January 2014 Cuperlo criticized the electoral reform proposed by Renzi in agreement with Berlusconi, but the proposal was overwhelmingly approved by the party's national board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The day after the vote, Cuperlo resigned from president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>After frequent calls by Renzi for a "new phase", on 13 February the national board decided to put an end to Letta's government and form a new one led by Renzi, as the latter had proposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Subsequently, on 22 February Renzi was sworn in as Prime Minister at the head of an identical coalition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On 28 February the PD officially joined the PES as a full member,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PES_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-PES-79">[79]</a></sup> ending a decade-long debate.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Premiership_of_Matteo_Renzi">Premiership of Matteo Renzi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Premiership of Matteo Renzi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Renzi_Cabinet" title="Renzi Cabinet">Renzi Cabinet</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (Italy)">2014 European Parliament election</a> the party obtained 40.8% of the vote and 31 seats. The party's score was virtually 15 percentage points up from five years before and the best result for an Italian party in a nationwide election since the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_1958" title="Italian general election, 1958">1958 general election</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a> won 42.4%. Also, the PD was the largest national party within the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">Parliament</a> in its <a href="/wiki/Eighth_European_Parliament" title="Eighth European Parliament">8th term</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Following his party's success, Renzi was able to secure the post of <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a> within the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> for <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a>, his minister of Foreign Affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015 <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Mattarella" title="Sergio Mattarella">Sergio Mattarella</a>, a veteran <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democrat</a> and founding member of the PD, whose candidacy had been proposed by Renzi and unanimously endorsed by the party's delegates, was elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Italy" title="President of Italy">President of Italy</a> during a <a href="/wiki/Italian_presidential_election,_2015" title="Italian presidential election, 2015">presidential election</a> triggered by President <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Napolitano" title="Giorgio Napolitano">Giorgio Napolitano</a>'s resignation.</p>
<p>During Renzi's first year as Prime Minister, several MPs defected from other parties to join the PD. They comprised splinters from SEL (most of whom led by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gennaro_Migliore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gennaro Migliore (page does not exist)">Gennaro Migliore</a>, see <a href="/wiki/Freedom_and_Rights" title="Freedom and Rights">Freedom and Rights</a>), SC (notably including <a href="/wiki/Stefania_Giannini" title="Stefania Giannini">Stefania Giannini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Ichino" title="Pietro Ichino">Pietro Ichino</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Andrea_Romano_(politician)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Andrea Romano (politician) (page does not exist)">Andrea Romano</a>), and the M5S. Consequently, the party increased its parliamentary numbers to 311 deputies and 114 senators by April 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Camera_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Camera-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Senato_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Senato-83">[83]</a></sup> Otherwise, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Cofferati" title="Sergio Cofferati">Sergio Cofferati</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Giuseppe Civati<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Fassina" title="Stefano Fassina">Stefano Fassina</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> left. They were the first and most notable splinters among the ranks of the party's internal left, but several others followed either Civati (who launched <a href="/wiki/Possible_(Italy)" title="Possible (Italy)">Possible</a>) or Fassina (who launched <a href="/wiki/Future_to_the_Left" title="Future to the Left">Future to the Left</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Left" title="Italian Left">Italian Left</a>) in the following months,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and, by May 2016, the PD's parliamentary numbers had gone down to 303 deputies and 114 senators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Camera_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Camera-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Senato_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-Senato-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Italian_regional_elections,_2015" title="Italian regional elections, 2015">2015 regional elections</a> Democratic Presidents were elected (or re-elected) in five regions out of seven: <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Rossi_(politician)" title="Enrico Rossi (politician)">Enrico Rossi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_regional_election,_2015" title="Tuscan regional election, 2015">Tuscany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luca_Ceriscioli" title="Luca Ceriscioli">Luca Ceriscioli</a> in <a href="/wiki/Marche_regional_election,_2015" title="Marche regional election, 2015">Marche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catiuscia_Marini" title="Catiuscia Marini">Catiuscia Marini</a> in <a href="/wiki/Umbrian_regional_election,_2015" title="Umbrian regional election, 2015">Umbria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_De_Luca" title="Vincenzo De Luca">Vincenzo De Luca</a> in <a href="/wiki/Campania_regional_election,_2015" title="Campania regional election, 2015">Campania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michele_Emiliano" title="Michele Emiliano">Michele Emiliano</a> in <a href="/wiki/Apulian_regional_election,_2015" title="Apulian regional election, 2015">Apulia</a>. As a result, 16 regions out of 20, including all those of central and southern Italy, were governed by the centre-left, while the opposition Lega Nord led Veneto and Lombardy, and propped up a centre-right government in Liguria.</p>
<p>After a huge defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_constitutional_referendum,_2016" title="Italian constitutional referendum, 2016">2016 constitutional referendum</a> (59.9% no, 40.1% yes), Renzi tendered his resignation as Prime Minister and was replaced by fellow Democrat <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Gentiloni_Cabinet" title="Gentiloni Cabinet">government</a>'s composition and coalition were very similar to those of the Renzi Cabinet. Following these developments there is expected to be a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2017" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2017">leadership election for the party in 2017</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology">Ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg/250px-Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg/375px-Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg/500px-Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Festa_dell%27Unit%C3%A0_Bologna_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Festa_de_l%27Unit%C3%A0" title="Festa de l'Unità">Festa de l'Unità</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a>, 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The PD is a <a href="/wiki/Big_tent" title="Big tent">big tent</a> <a href="/wiki/Centre-left_politics" title="Centre-left politics">centre-left</a> party, influenced by the ideas of <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Christian_left" title="Christian left">Christian left</a>. The common roots of the founding components of the party reside in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement" title="Italian resistance movement">Italian resistance movement</a>, the writing of <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Italy" title="Constitution of Italy">Italian Constitution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Historic_Compromise" title="Historic Compromise">Historic Compromise</a>, all three events which saw the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Italian Communist Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a> (the two major forerunners of the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> and <a href="/wiki/Democracy_is_Freedom_%E2%80%93_The_Daisy" title="Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy">Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy</a>, respectively) cooperate. The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Liberalism in the United States">American liberalism</a> are also important sources of inspiration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In a 2008 interview to <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El País">El País</a></i>, Veltroni, who can be considered the main founding father of the party, clearly stated that the PD should be considered a "<a href="/wiki/Reformism" title="Reformism">reformist</a>" party and could not be linked to the traditional values of the <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>The party stresses national and social cohesion, <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressivism</a>, a moderate <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">social liberalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">green</a> issues, <a href="/wiki/Progressive_tax" title="Progressive tax">progressive taxation</a> and (<a href="/wiki/Pro-Europeanism" title="Pro-Europeanism">pro</a>-)<a href="/wiki/Europeanism" title="Europeanism">Europeanism</a>. In this respect, the party's precursors strongly supported the need of balancing budgets in order to comply to <a href="/wiki/Euro_convergence_criteria" title="Euro convergence criteria">Maastricht criteria</a>. Under Veltroni and, more recently, Renzi, the party took a strong stance in favour of constitutional reform and of a new electoral law, on the road toward a <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">two-party system</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideological_trends">Ideological trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ideological trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The PD is a plural party, including several distinct ideological trends:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social democracy</a>.</b> The bulk of the party, including many former <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a>, is social-democratic and emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_issue" title="Social issue">social issues</a>. There are however traditional social democrats, led by <a href="/wiki/Massimo_D%27Alema" title="Massimo D'Alema">Massimo D'Alema</a> (hence <i><a href="/wiki/Dalemiani" title="Dalemiani">Dalemiani</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a> (hence <i><a href="/wiki/Bersaniani" title="Bersaniani">Bersaniani</a></i>), and <a href="/wiki/Third_Way" title="Third Way">Third Way</a> types, led by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a> (hence <i><a href="/wiki/Veltroniani" title="Veltroniani">Veltroniani</a></i>, organised in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Movement_(Italy)" title="Democratic Movement (Italy)">Democratic Movement</a>). While the former are supportive of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialism" title="Democratic socialism">democratic socialism</a> (and thus in favour of a close cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Left_Ecology_Freedom" title="Left Ecology Freedom">Left Ecology Freedom</a>), the latter are strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Liberalism in the United States">American liberalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a> ideas.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Christian_left" title="Christian left">Christian left</a>.</b> The party includes many <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>-inspired members, most of whom come from the left-wing of the late <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a> (having later joined <a href="/wiki/Democracy_is_Freedom_%E2%80%93_The_Daisy" title="Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy">Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy</a>). "Democratic Catholics" are organised in several factions, including <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a>'s <a href="/wiki/360_Association" title="360 Association">360 Association</a> (also <i><a href="/wiki/Lettiani" title="Lettiani">Lettiani</a></i>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democrats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrists</a>), <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Fioroni" title="Giuseppe Fioroni">Giuseppe Fioroni</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Populars" title="The Populars">Populars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Democrats_Really" title="Democrats Really">Democrats Really</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Christians" title="Social Christians">Social Christians</a> (who adhere to <a href="/wiki/Christian_socialism" title="Christian socialism">Christian socialism</a>).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">Social liberalism</a>.</b> It is endorsed mainly by former members of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Republican_Party" title="Italian Republican Party">Italian Republican Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Liberal_Party" title="Italian Liberal Party">Italian Liberal Party</a>, who are organised in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_PD" title="Liberal PD">Liberal PD</a> faction.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green politics</a>.</b> It is endorsed mainly by former members of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_Greens" title="Federation of the Greens">Federation of the Greens</a> and other greens, who have jointly formed the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Ecologists" title="Democratic Ecologists">Democratic Ecologists</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is not an easy task to include the trend represented by <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, whose supporters have been known as "Big Bangers", "Now!" or, more frequently, <i><a href="/wiki/Renziani" title="Renziani">Renziani</a></i>, in any of the categories above. The nature of Renzi's <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressivism</a> is a matter of debate and has been linked both to <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Populism" title="Populism">populism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ricerca.repubblica.it_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-ricerca.repubblica.it-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ricerca.repubblica.it_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-ricerca.repubblica.it-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> According to Maria Teresa Meli of <i><a href="/wiki/Corriere_della_Sera" title="Corriere della Sera">Corriere della Sera</a></i>, Renzi "pursues a precise model, borrowed from the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>", comprising "a strange mix (for Italy) of liberal policies in the economic sphere and populism. This means that, on one side, he will attack the privileges of trade unions, especially of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_General_Confederation_of_Labour" title="Italian General Confederation of Labour">CGIL</a>, which defends only the already protected, while, on the other, he will sharply attack the vested powers, bankers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confindustria" title="Confindustria">Confindustria</a> and a certain type of capitalism [...]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_affiliation">International affiliation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International affiliation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>International affiliation was quite a controversial issue for the PD in its early days and, in fact, it was settled only in 2014.</p>
<p>The debate on which <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a> to join saw the former <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> generally in favour of the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a> (PES) and most former members of <a href="/wiki/Democracy_is_Freedom_%E2%80%93_The_Daisy" title="Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy">Democracy is Freedom – The Daisy</a> in favour of the <a href="/wiki/European_Democratic_Party" title="European Democratic Party">European Democratic Party</a> (EDP), a component of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Group" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe Group">Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe</a> (ALDE) Group. After the party's formation in 2007, the new party's MEPs continued to sit with the PES and ALDE groups to which their former parties had been elected during the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2004_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2004 (Italy)">2004 European Parliament election</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (Italy)">2009 European Parliament election</a>, the party's 21 MEPs chose to unite for the new term within the <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">European parliamentary group</a> of the PES, which was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats</a> (S&amp;D).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viola2015_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Viola2015-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 December 2012 PD leader <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a> attended in Rome to the founding convention of the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance" title="Progressive Alliance">Progressive Alliance</a> (PA), a nascent <a href="/wiki/Political_international" title="Political international">political international</a> for parties dissatisfied with the continued admittance and inclusion of authoritarian movements into the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_International" title="Socialist International">Socialist International</a> (SI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> On 22 May 2013 the PD was a founding member of the PA at the international's official inauguration in <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> on the eve of the 150th anniversary of the formation of the <a href="/wiki/General_German_Workers%27_Association" title="General German Workers' Association">General German Workers' Association</a>, the oldest of the two parties which merged in 1875 in order to form the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_(12899722993).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2424" data-file-width="3780" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_%2812899722993%29.jpg/250px-PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_%2812899722993%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_%2812899722993%29.jpg/375px-PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_%2812899722993%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_%2812899722993%29.jpg/500px-PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_%2812899722993%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PES-Kongress_mit_Bundeskanzler_Werner_Faymann_in_Rom_(12899722993).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a> speaks at the congress of the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, a centrist who has led the party since 2013, wanted the party to join both the SI and the PES.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> On 20 February 2014 the PD leadership applied for full membership of the PES.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In Renzi's view, the party would count more as a member of a major European party and, within the PES, it would join forces with alike parties such as the British <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>. On 28 February the PD was welcomed as a full member into the PES.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PES_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-PES-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Factions">Factions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Factions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The PD includes several internal factions, most of which trace the previous allegiances of party members. Factions form different alliances depending on the issues and some party members have multiple factional allegiances.</p>
