<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_leadership_election">2007 leadership election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2007 leadership election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2007" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2007">Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2007</a></div>
<p>After the election, which saw the victory of <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a>, the party's internal composition was as follows:</p>
<dl>
<dt>Majority led by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a> (75.8%)</dt>
</dl>
<p>Three national lists supported the candidacy of Veltroni. The bulk of the former <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Veltroniani" title="Veltroniani">Veltroniani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dalemiani" title="Dalemiani">Dalemiani</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fassiniani" title="Fassiniani">Fassiniani</a></i>), the <i><a href="/wiki/Rutelliani" title="Rutelliani">Rutelliani</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Rutelli" title="Francesco Rutelli">Francesco Rutelli</a> (including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theo-Dem" title="Theo-Dem">Theo-Dem</a>), <a href="/wiki/The_Populars" title="The Populars">The Populars</a> of <a href="/wiki/Franco_Marini" title="Franco Marini">Franco Marini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_PD" title="Liberal PD">Liberal PD</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Social_Christians" title="Social Christians">Social Christians</a> and smaller groups (<a href="/wiki/Middle_Italy_(political_party)" title="Middle Italy (political party)">Middle Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Republicans_Movement" title="European Republicans Movement">European Republicans Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reformist_Alliance" title="Reformist Alliance">Reformist Alliance</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Reformists_for_Europe" title="Reformists for Europe">Reformists for Europe</a>) formed a joint-list named "Democrats with Veltroni" (43.7%). The <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Ecologists" title="Democratic Ecologists">Democratic Ecologists</a> of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ermete_Realacci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ermete Realacci (page does not exist)">Ermete Realacci</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/Giovanna_Melandri" title="Giovanna Melandri">Giovanna Melandri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Damiano" title="Cesare Damiano">Cesare Damiano</a>, formed "Environment, Innovation and Labour" (8.1%). The <a href="/wiki/Democrats,_Laicists,_Socialists" title="Democrats, Laicists, Socialists">Democrats, Laicists, Socialists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Say_Left" title="Say Left">Say Left</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Federation_(Italy)" title="Labour Federation (Italy)">Labourites – Liberal Socialists</a> presented a list named "<a href="/wiki/To_the_Left" title="To the Left">To the Left</a>" (7.7%). Local lists in support of Veltroni got 16.4%.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Minorities led by <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a> (12.9%) and <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a> (11.0%)</dt>
</dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Olivists" title="Olivists">Olivists</a>, whose members were staunch supporters of <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>, divided in two camps. The largest one, including <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Parisi" title="Arturo Parisi">Arturo Parisi</a>, endorsed <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a>, while a smaller one, including <a href="/wiki/Paolo_De_Castro" title="Paolo De Castro">Paolo De Castro</a>, endorsed <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Paolo_De_Castro" title="Paolo De Castro">Paolo De Castro</a>. Bindi benefited also from the support of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Agazio_Loiero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Agazio Loiero (page does not exist)">Agazio Loiero</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Southern_Democratic_Party" title="Southern Democratic Party">Southern Democratic Party</a>, while Letta was endorsed by <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Dellai" title="Lorenzo Dellai">Lorenzo Dellai</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Daisy_Civic_List" title="Daisy Civic List">Daisy Civic List</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renato_Soru" title="Renato Soru">Renato Soru</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sardinia_Project" title="Sardinia Project">Sardinia Project</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Pittella" title="Gianni Pittella">Gianni Pittella</a>'s social democrats.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_leadership_election">2009 leadership election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2009 leadership election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2009" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2009">Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2009</a></div>
<p>After the election, which saw the victory of <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a>, the party's internal composition was as follows:</p>
<dl>
<dt>Majority led by <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a> (53.2%)</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Bersaniani" title="Bersaniani">Bersaniani</a></b></i> and <i><b><a href="/wiki/Dalemiani" title="Dalemiani">Dalemiani</a></b></i>: the social-democratic groups around Bersani and <a href="/wiki/Massimo_D%27Alema" title="Massimo D'Alema">Massimo D'Alema</a> (who wants the PD to be a traditional centre-left party in the European social-democratic tradition); D'Alema organized his faction as <b><a href="/wiki/Reformists_and_Democrats" title="Reformists and Democrats">Reformists and Democrats</a></b>, welcoming also some <i>Lettiani</i> and some Populars.</li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Lettiani" title="Lettiani">Lettiani</a></b></i>: the centrist group around <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a>, known also as <b><a href="/wiki/360_Association" title="360 Association">360 Association</a></b>; its members are keen supporters of an alliance with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Centre_(2008)" title="Union of the Centre (2008)">Union of the Centre</a>, similarly to what also D'Alema proposes.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/To_the_Left" title="To the Left">To the Left</a></b>: the social-democratic and democratic-socialist internal left led by <a href="/wiki/Livia_Turco" title="Livia Turco">Livia Turco</a>;</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Democrats_Really" title="Democrats Really">Democrats Really</a></b>: the group around <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a> and composed mainly of the left-wing members of the late <a href="/wiki/Italian_People%27s_Party_(1994)" title="Italian People's Party (1994)">Italian People's Party</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Social_Christians" title="Social Christians">Social Christians</a></b>: a Christian social-democratic group, that was a founding component of the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Democracy_and_Socialism" title="Democracy and Socialism">Democracy and Socialism</a></b>: a social-democratic group of splinters from the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party_(2007)" title="Italian Socialist Party (2007)">Socialist Party</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Gavino_Angius" title="Gavino Angius">Gavino Angius</a>.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Area" title="Democratic Area">Democratic Area</a>, minority led by <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a> (34.3%)</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Veltroniani" title="Veltroniani">Veltroniani</a></b></i>: followers of <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a>, basically social democrats coming from the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a> who support the so-called "majoritarian vocation" of the party, the selection of party candidates and leaders through primaries and a <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">two-party system</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/The_Populars" title="The Populars">Populars</a>/<a href="/wiki/Fourth_Phase" title="Fourth Phase">Fourth Phase</a></b>: heirs of the <a href="/wiki/Christian_left" title="Christian left">Christian left</a> tradition of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_People%27s_Party_(1994)" title="Italian People's Party (1994)">Italian People's Party</a> and of the left wing of the late <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a>.</li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Rutelliani" title="Rutelliani">Rutelliani</a></b></i>: centrists and liberals gathered around <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Rutelli" title="Francesco Rutelli">Francesco Rutelli</a>, known also as <b><a href="/wiki/Free_Democrats_(Italy)" title="Free Democrats (Italy)">Free Democrats</a></b>; most of them left after Bersani's victory to form the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Italy" title="Alliance for Italy">Alliance for Italy</a>, while a minority (<a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ermete_Realacci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ermete Realacci (page does not exist)">Ermete Realacci</a>, etc.) chose to stay.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Simply_Democrats" title="Simply Democrats">Simply Democrats</a></b>: a list promoted by a diverse group of leading Democrats (<a href="/wiki/Debora_Serracchiani" title="Debora Serracchiani">Debora Serracchiani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_Borsellino" title="Rita Borsellino">Rita Borsellino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Cofferati" title="Sergio Cofferati">Sergio Cofferati</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=David_Sassoli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="David Sassoli (page does not exist)">David Sassoli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francesca_Barracciu" title="Francesca Barracciu">Francesca Barracciu</a>) who were committed to renewal in party leadership and cleanliness of party elects.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Liberal_PD" title="Liberal PD">Liberal PD</a></b>: the liberal (mostly social-liberal) faction of the PD led by <a href="/wiki/Valerio_Zanone" title="Valerio Zanone">Valerio Zanone</a>; its members have been close to Veltroni and Rutelli.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Ecologists" title="Democratic Ecologists">Democratic Ecologists</a></b>: the green faction of the PD led by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ermete_Realacci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ermete Realacci (page does not exist)">Ermete Realacci</a>; its members have been close to Veltroni and Rutelli.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Theo-Dems" title="Theo-Dems">Theo-Dems</a></b>: a tiny Christian-democratic group representing the right-wing of the party on social issues, albeit being progressive on economic ones; most Theo-Dems, including their leader <a href="/wiki/Paola_Binetti" title="Paola Binetti">Paola Binetti</a>, left the PD in 2009–2010 in order to join the UdC or the ApI, while others, led by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luigi_Bobba&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luigi Bobba (page does not exist)">Luigi Bobba</a>, chose to stay.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Minority led by <a href="/wiki/Ignazio_Marino" title="Ignazio Marino">Ignazio Marino</a> (12.5%)</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>un-affiliated social liberals, social democrats and supporters of a broad alliance including <a href="/wiki/Italy_of_Values" title="Italy of Values">Italy of Values</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Radicals" title="Italian Radicals">Radicals</a> and the parties to the left of the PD; after the election, most of them joined Marino in an association named <a href="/wiki/Change_Italy" title="Change Italy">Change Italy</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Democrats_in_Network" title="Democrats in Network">Democrats in Network</a></b>: a social-democratic faction of former <i>Veltroniani</i> led by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Goffredo_Bettini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Goffredo Bettini (page does not exist)">Goffredo Bettini</a>.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Non-aligned factions</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Olivists" title="Olivists">Olivists</a></b>: followers of <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a> who want the party to be stuck in the tradition of <a href="/wiki/The_Olive_Tree_(Italy)" title="The Olive Tree (Italy)">The Olive Tree</a>; the group, which includes both Christian left exponents and social democrats is led by <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Parisi" title="Arturo Parisi">Arturo Parisi</a>. Most Olivists supported Bersani, while Parisi endorsed Franceschini.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.932013_developments">2010–2013 developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2010–2013 developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the summer of 2010 <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a>, leader of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Area" title="Democratic Area">Democratic Area</a> (the largest minority faction), and <a href="/wiki/Piero_Fassino" title="Piero Fassino">Piero Fassino</a> re-approached with <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a> and joined the party majority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere_16-09-2010_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere_16-09-2010-108">[108]</a></sup> As a response, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a> formed <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Movement_(Italy)" title="Democratic Movement (Italy)">Democratic Movement</a> to defend the "original spirit" of the PD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere_16-09-2010_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere_16-09-2010-108">[108]</a></sup> In doing this he was supported by 75 deputies: 33 <i><a href="/wiki/Veltroniani" title="Veltroniani">Veltroniani</a></i>, 35 <a href="/wiki/The_Populars" title="The Populars">Populars</a> close to <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Fioroni" title="Giuseppe Fioroni">Giuseppe Fioroni</a> and 7 former <i><a href="/wiki/Rutelliani" title="Rutelliani">Rutelliani</a></i> led by <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Some pundits hinted that the Bersani-Franceschini pact was envisioned in order both to marginalise Veltroni and to reduce the influence of <a href="/wiki/Massimo_D%27Alema" title="Massimo D'Alema">Massimo D'Alema</a>, the party bigwig behind Bersani, whose 2009 bid was supported primarily by <i><a href="/wiki/Dalemiani" title="Dalemiani">Dalemiani</a></i>. Veltroni and D'Alema had been long-time rivals within the centre-left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of September the party's majority was composed of those who supported Bersani since the beginning (divided in five main factions: <i><a href="/wiki/Bersaniani" title="Bersaniani">Bersaniani</a></i>, <i>Dalemiani</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lettiani" title="Lettiani">Lettiani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Democrats_Really" title="Democrats Really">Bindiani</a></i> and the party's left-wing) and Democratic Area of Franceschini and Fassino. Then, there were two minority coalitions: Veltroni's Democratic Movement (<i>Veltroniani</i>, Fioroni's Populars, ex-<i>Rutelliani</i>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Ecologists" title="Democratic Ecologists">Democratic Ecologists</a> and a majority of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_PD" title="Liberal PD">Liberal PD</a> members) and <a href="/wiki/Change_Italy" title="Change Italy">Change Italy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ignazio_Marino" title="Ignazio Marino">Ignazio Marino</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Corriere_della_Sera" title="Corriere della Sera">Corriere della Sera</a></i>, in November 2011 the party was divided mainly in three ideological camps battling for its soul:</p>
<ul>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialism" title="Democratic socialism">socialist</a> left: the <a href="/wiki/Remake_Italy" title="Remake Italy">Young Turks</a> (mostly supporters of Bersani, as <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Fassina" title="Stefano Fassina">Stefano Fassina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Orfini" title="Matteo Orfini">Matteo Orfini</a>);</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a> centre: it includes Bersani's core supporters (<i>Bersaniani</i>, <i>Dalemiani</i>, <i>Bindiani</i>);</li>
<li>a "new right": <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Renziani" title="Renziani">faction</a>, proposing an overtly <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> political line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Since November 2011 similar differences surfaced in the party over <a href="/wiki/Monti_Cabinet" title="Monti Cabinet">Monti Cabinet</a>: while the party's right-wing, especially Liberal PD, was enthusiastic in its support, Fassina and other leftists, especially those linked to trade unions, were critical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In February 2012 Fassina published a book in which he described his view as "neo-labourite humanism" and explained it in connection with <a href="/wiki/Catholic_social_teaching" title="Catholic social teaching">Catholic social teaching</a>, saying that his "neo-labourism" was designed to attract Catholic voters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Once again, his opposition to <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economic liberalism</a> was strongly criticized by the party's right-wing as well as by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stefano_Ceccanti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stefano Ceccanti (page does not exist)">Stefano Ceccanti</a>, a leading Catholic in the party and supporter of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a>, who said that a leftist platform <i>à la</i> Fassina would never win back the Catholic vote in places like <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to YouTrend, a website, 35% of the Democratic deputies and senators elected in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2013" title="Italian general election, 2013">2013 general election</a> were <i><a href="/wiki/Bersaniani" title="Bersaniani">Bersaniani</a></i>, 23% members of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Area" title="Democratic Area">Democratic Area</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Movement_(Italy)" title="Democratic Movement (Italy)">Democratic Movement</a>), 13% <i><a href="/wiki/Renziani" title="Renziani">Renziani</a></i>, 6% <i><a href="/wiki/360_Association" title="360 Association">Lettiani</a></i>, 4.5% <i><a href="/wiki/Dalemiani" title="Dalemiani">Dalemiani</a></i>, 4.5% <a href="/wiki/Remake_Italy" title="Remake Italy">Young Turks / Remake Italy</a>, 2% <i><a href="/wiki/Democrats_Really" title="Democrats Really">Bindiani</a></i> and 1.5% <i><a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Civati" title="Giuseppe Civati">Civatiani</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the party performed below expectations, more Democrats started to look at Renzi, who had been defeated by Bersani in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_centre-left_primary_election,_2012" title="Italian centre-left primary election, 2012">2012 primary election</a> to select the centre-left's candidate for Prime Minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meli-03.08.2013_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Meli-03.08.2013-123">[123]</a></sup> In early September, two leading centrists, Franceschini and Fioroni, leaders of Democratic Area and The Populars, endorsed Renzi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere-2013-09-03_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere-2013-09-03-124">[124]</a></sup> Also two former leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_of_the_Left" title="Democrats of the Left">Democrats of the Left</a>, Veltroni and Fassino,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere-2013-09-04_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere-2013-09-04-125">[125]</a></sup> decided to support Renzi, while a third, D'Alema, endorsed <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Cuperlo" title="Gianni Cuperlo">Gianni Cuperlo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October four candidates filed their bid to become secretary: Renzi, Cuperlo, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Civati" title="Giuseppe Civati">Pippo Civati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Pittella" title="Gianni Pittella">Gianni Pittella</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Repubblica-2013-10-11_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Repubblica-2013-10-11-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_leadership_election">2013 leadership election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2013 leadership election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)_leadership_election,_2013" title="Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2013">Democratic Party (Italy) leadership election, 2013</a></div>
<p>After the election, which saw the victory of <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, the party's internal composition was as follows:</p>
<dl>
<dt>Majority led by <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a> (67.6%)</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Renziani" title="Renziani">Renziani</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Area" title="Democratic Area">Democratic Area</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Veltroniani" title="Veltroniani">Veltroniani</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere-2013-09-04_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere-2013-09-04-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Populars" title="The Populars">The Populars</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere-2013-09-03_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere-2013-09-03-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Liberal_PD" title="Liberal PD">Liberal PD</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> most <i><a href="/wiki/Lettiani" title="Lettiani">Lettiani</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> most <a href="/wiki/Olivists" title="Olivists">Olivists</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Ecologists" title="Democratic Ecologists">Democratic Ecologists</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Minority led by <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Cuperlo" title="Gianni Cuperlo">Gianni Cuperlo</a> (18.2%)</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bersaniani" title="Bersaniani">Bersaniani</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Repubblica-2013-09-14_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Repubblica-2013-09-14-134">[134]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Dalemiani" title="Dalemiani">Dalemiani</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Repubblica-2013-09-14_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Repubblica-2013-09-14-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere-2013-09-23_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere-2013-09-23-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Remake_Italy" title="Remake Italy">Young Turks / Remake Italy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Repubblica-2013-09-14_134-2"><a href="#cite_note-Repubblica-2013-09-14-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corriere-2013-09-23_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corriere-2013-09-23-135">[135]</a></sup> most <a href="/wiki/Democrats_Really" title="Democrats Really">Democrats Really</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Minority led by <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Civati" title="Giuseppe Civati">Pippo Civati</a> (14.2%)</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pippo_Civati" title="Pippo Civati">Civatiani</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Puppato" title="Laura Puppato">Laura Puppato</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuova_Venezia_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nuova_Venezia-137">[137]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Felice_Casson" title="Felice Casson">Felice Casson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuova_Venezia_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nuova_Venezia-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.932016_alignments">2014–2016 alignments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2014–2016 alignments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After 2013 leadership election, the party's main factions<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> have been the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Renziani" title="Renziani">Renziani</a>.</b></i> The group around <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, PD leader and Prime Minister, and a <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_Way" title="Third Way">Third Way</a>-oriented and modernising faction. It is thus considered the right-wing of the party, but also represents its majority. <i>Renziani</i> support a <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">two-party system</a> and the so-called "majoritarian vocation" of the PD, through the formation of a "party of the nation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Prominent members of the faction are <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luca_Lotti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luca Lotti (page does not exist)">Luca Lotti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Elena_Boschi" title="Maria Elena Boschi">Maria Elena Boschi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graziano_Delrio" title="Graziano Delrio">Graziano Delrio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Guerini" title="Lorenzo Guerini">Lorenzo Guerini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Bonaccini" title="Stefano Bonaccini">Stefano Bonaccini</a>. The faction has a <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian-democratic</a> section, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Space" title="Democratic Space">Democratic Space</a>, which is led by Delrio and Guerini. Also another group of Christian democrats, <a href="/wiki/The_Populars" title="The Populars">The Populars</a> of <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Fioroni" title="Giuseppe Fioroni">Giuseppe Fioroni</a>, are affiliated. According to news sources, as of December 2016, full-fledged <i>Renziani</i> count 50 MPs, The Populars 30 and other <i>Renziani</i> 25, for a total of 105.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Area" title="Democratic Area">Democratic Area</a>.</b> A mainly <a href="/wiki/Christian_left" title="Christian left">Christian leftist</a> faction, with roots in <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a>'s left-wing and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_People%27s_Party_(1994)" title="Italian People's Party (1994)">Italian People's Party</a>. Led by <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a>, it notably includes <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luigi_Zanda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luigi Zanda (page does not exist)">Luigi Zanda</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ettore_Rosato&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ettore Rosato (page does not exist)">Ettore Rosato</a>, as well as prominent social democrats like <a href="/wiki/Piero_Fassino" title="Piero Fassino">Piero Fassino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Debora_Serracchiani" title="Debora Serracchiani">Debora Serracchiani</a>, for a total of 90 MPs.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Left_is_Change" title="Left is Change">Left is Change</a>.</b> A social-democratic faction led by <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Martina" title="Maurizio Martina">Maurizio Martina</a>. Most of its members were affiliated with Reformist Area (see below), but split in order to support Renzi. The faction, which includes, among others, <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Damiano" title="Cesare Damiano">Cesare Damiano</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vannino_Chiti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vannino Chiti (page does not exist)">Vannino Chiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anna_Finocchiaro" title="Anna Finocchiaro">Anna Finocchiaro</a>, counts 70 MPs.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Remake_Italy" title="Remake Italy">Remake Italy</a>.</b> A social-democratic faction loyal to Renzi. Led by <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Orfini" title="Matteo Orfini">Matteo Orfini</a>, the party's president, and <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Orlando" title="Andrea Orlando">Andrea Orlando</a>, it counts 60 MPs.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Reformist_Area" title="Reformist Area">Reformist Area</a>/Left.</b> Inspired by traditional <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialism" title="Democratic socialism">democratic socialism</a>, it is the main left-wing of the party. It was formed by the majority of <i><a href="/wiki/Bersaniani" title="Bersaniani">Bersaniani</a></i>, loyalists former secretary <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a>. The faction's leader is <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Speranza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roberto Speranza (page does not exist)">Roberto Speranza</a>. The Reformists often oppose Renzi's politicies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Other than Speranza and Bersani, the faction notably includes <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Epifani" title="Guglielmo Epifani">Guglielmo Epifani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a> (whose sub-faction is named <a href="/wiki/Democrats_Really" title="Democrats Really">Democrats Really</a>), and counts 60 MPs.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/LeftDem" title="LeftDem">LeftDem</a>.</b> Led by <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Cuperlo" title="Gianni Cuperlo">Gianni Cuperlo</a>, it is another minority social-democratic faction, including 15 MPs.</li>
</ul>
<p>A more complete list of PD's factions is available in the following table:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_support">Popular support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Popular support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Italian_Regions_Party.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2032" data-file-width="1632" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Italian_Regions_Party.png/250px-Italian_Regions_Party.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Italian_Regions_Party.png/375px-Italian_Regions_Party.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Italian_Regions_Party.png/500px-Italian_Regions_Party.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Italian_Regions_Party.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Italy" title="Regions of Italy">Regions of Italy</a>: the 15 (out of 20) regions governed by Democratic Presidents are in red.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The PD, as previously the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Italian Communist Party</a> (PCI), has its strongholds in <a href="/wiki/Central_Italy" title="Central Italy">Central Italy</a> and big cities.</p>
<p>The party runs fifteen <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Italy" title="Regions of Italy">regions</a> out of twenty and the cities of <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bari" title="Bari">Bari</a>. It also takes part to the government of the region of <a href="/wiki/Trentino-Alto_Adige/S%C3%BCdtirol" title="Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol">Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol</a>, as well as the cities of <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cagliari" title="Cagliari">Cagliari</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2008" title="Italian general election, 2008">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_2013" title="Italian general election, 2013">2013 general elections</a> the PD obtained its best results in <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a> (46.8% and 37.5%), <a href="/wiki/Emilia-Romagna" title="Emilia-Romagna">Emilia-Romagna</a> (45.7% and 37.0%), <a href="/wiki/Umbria" title="Umbria">Umbria</a> (44.4% and 32.1%), <a href="/wiki/Marche" title="Marche">Marche</a> (41.4% and 27.7%), <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a> (37.6% and 27.7%) and <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a> (36.8% and 25.7%). Democrats are generally stronger in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">North</a> than the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">South</a>, with the sole exception of <a href="/wiki/Basilicata" title="Basilicata">Basilicata</a> (38.6% in 2008 and 25.7% in 2013),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> where the party has drawn most of its personnel from <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democracy</a> (DC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(Italy)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (Italy)">2014 European Parliament election</a> gave a thumping 40.8% of the vote to the party, which was the first Italian party to get more than 40% of the vote in a nationwide election since DC won 42.4% of the vote in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_1958" title="Italian general election, 1958">1958 general election</a>. In 2014, as usual, the PD did better in Tuscany (56.6%), Emilia-Romagna (52.5%) and Umbria (49.2%), but made significant gains in <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a> (40.3%, +19.0% from 2009), <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> (37.5%, +17.2%) and the South.</p>
<p>The electoral results of the PD in the 10 most populated regions of Italy are shown in the table below.</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
<tr>
<td></td>
<td><b>2008 general</b></td>
<td><b>2009 European</b></td>
<td><b>2010 regional</b></td>
<td><b>2013 general</b></td>
<td><b>2014 European</b></td>
<td><b>2015 regional</b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Piedmont</b></td>
<td>32.4</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Party_(Italy)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Secretary: <a href="/wiki/Walter_Veltroni" title="Walter Veltroni">Walter Veltroni</a> (2007–2009), <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a> (2009), <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_Bersani" title="Pier Luigi Bersani">Pier Luigi Bersani</a> (2009–2013), <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Epifani" title="Guglielmo Epifani">Guglielmo Epifani</a> (2013), <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a> (2013–present)
<ul>
<li>Deputy Secretary: <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a> (2007–2009), <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Letta" title="Enrico Letta">Enrico Letta</a> (2009–2013), <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Guerini" title="Lorenzo Guerini">Lorenzo Guerini</a> (2014–present), <a href="/wiki/Debora_Serracchiani" title="Debora Serracchiani">Debora Serracchiani</a> (2014–present)</li>
<li>Coordinator of the Secretariat: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Goffredo_Bettini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Goffredo Bettini (page does not exist)">Goffredo Bettini</a> (2007–2009), <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Migliavacca" title="Maurizio Migliavacca">Maurizio Migliavacca</a> (2009–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luca_Lotti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luca Lotti (page does not exist)">Luca Lotti</a> (2013–2014), <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Guerini" title="Lorenzo Guerini">Lorenzo Guerini</a> (2014–present)</li>
<li>Organizational Secretary: <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Fioroni" title="Giuseppe Fioroni">Giuseppe Fioroni</a> (2007–2009), <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Migliavacca" title="Maurizio Migliavacca">Maurizio Migliavacca</a> (2009), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nico_Stumpo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nico Stumpo (page does not exist)">Nico Stumpo</a> (2009–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Davide_Zoggia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Davide Zoggia (page does not exist)">Davide Zoggia</a> (2013–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luca_Lotti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luca Lotti (page does not exist)">Luca Lotti</a> (2013–2014), <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Guerini" title="Lorenzo Guerini">Lorenzo Guerini</a> (2014–present)</li>
<li>Spokesperson: <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Orlando" title="Andrea Orlando">Andrea Orlando</a> (2008–2013), <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Guerini" title="Lorenzo Guerini">Lorenzo Guerini</a> (2013–2014), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alessia_Rotta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alessia Rotta (page does not exist)">Alessia Rotta</a> (2014–present)</li>
<li>Treasurer: <a href="/wiki/Mauro_Agostini" title="Mauro Agostini">Mauro Agostini</a> (2007–2009), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Antonio_Misiani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Antonio Misiani (page does not exist)">Antonio Misiani</a> (2009–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Francesco_Bonifazi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Francesco Bonifazi (page does not exist)">Francesco Bonifazi</a> (2013–present)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>President: <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a> (2007–2008), <a href="/wiki/Anna_Finocchiaro" title="Anna Finocchiaro">Anna Finocchiaro</a> (acting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> 2008–2009), <a href="/wiki/Rosy_Bindi" title="Rosy Bindi">Rosy Bindi</a> (2009–2013), <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Cuperlo" title="Gianni Cuperlo">Gianni Cuperlo</a> (2013–2014), <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Orfini" title="Matteo Orfini">Matteo Orfini</a> (2014–present)
<ul>
<li>Vice President: <a href="/wiki/Marina_Sereni" title="Marina Sereni">Marina Sereni</a> (2009–2013), <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Scalfarotto" title="Ivan Scalfarotto">Ivan Scalfarotto</a> (2009–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Matteo_Ricci_(politician)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Matteo Ricci (politician) (page does not exist)">Matteo Ricci</a> (2013–present), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sandra_Zampa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sandra Zampa (page does not exist)">Sandra Zampa</a> (2013–present)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Party Leader in the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Italy)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Italy)">Chamber of Deputies</a>: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Antonello_Soro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Antonello Soro (page does not exist)">Antonello Soro</a> (2007–2009), <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franceschini" title="Dario Franceschini">Dario Franceschini</a> (2009–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Speranza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roberto Speranza (page does not exist)">Roberto Speranza</a> (2013–2015), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ettore_Rosato&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ettore Rosato (page does not exist)">Ettore Rosato</a> (2015–present)</li>
<li>Party Leader in the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Republic_(Italy)" title="Senate of the Republic (Italy)">Senate</a>: <a href="/wiki/Anna_Finocchiaro" title="Anna Finocchiaro">Anna Finocchiaro</a> (2007–2013), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luigi_Zanda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luigi Zanda (page does not exist)">Luigi Zanda</a> (2013–present)</li>
<li>Party Leader in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=David_Sassoli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="David Sassoli (page does not exist)">David Sassoli</a> (2009–2014), <a href="/wiki/Patrizia_Toia" title="Patrizia Toia">Patrizia Toia</a> (2014–present)</li>
</ul>
